-113 -                    ANNEX 7
ANNEX 7: ENVIRONMENTAL ASSESSMENT SUMMARY
Introduction
1.    Shandong is located in the northeast of China and is bordered to the north by
Hebei Province, to the south by Anhui and Jiangsu Provinces, to the east by the Bohai
Sea and to the west by Hebei and Henan Provinces. The province covers an area of
157,000 km2 and has a population of 87 million (1995 data), of which the urban
population accounted for 32 percent. The population growth rate is 0.38 percent. Jinan,
the provincial capital, has a total population of 5.37 million, of which the urban area
population is 2.43 million, and is one of the major industrial centers of the province,
accounting for about 10 percent of its GDP.
2.   Industrial sectors represented in Jinan include steel, machinery, metals, textiles,
food, chemicals and pharmaceuticals. Industrial growth in Jinan has been rapid, with
output rising in real terms by a factor of 2.5 between 1986 and 1994. Other major cities
in Shandong include Qingdao, Dongying, Zibo, Weihai and Yantai. Each of these cities
has a per capita GDP in the highest 10 percent of all cities in China, although that of
Jinan is the lowest of the major cities in Shandong. The rapid growth in the major cities
in Shandong has resulted in serious environmental problems, in particular in relation to
air pollution.
3.    The Xiaoqing River Basin (XRB) covers an area of approximately 16,992 km2
and a population in the order of 9 million, some 10 percent of the provincial total. The
basin is an important agricultural and industrial production base for Shandong Province,
accounting for one-fifth of the provincial GDP.
4.    Rapid industrial growth in the Xiaoqing basin has led to a major decline in water
quality, and pollution in the Basin poses threats to health and to economic development.
Increasingly there are reports of unsafe drinking water, and contamination of Laizhou
Bay threatens the key seafood industry of Shandong, to which there has already been
substantial damage.
5.    Weihai and Yantai are both located in the northeastern part of the Shandong
peninsula on the Yellow Sea coast. Weihai has a population of 2.4 million, of which
420,000 are urban; the urban center includes industrial areas and the suburban population
is mainly engaged in agriculture, fisheries and aquaculture. A high-tech industrial zone is
planned for the southern part of the city. Yantai is an important port city with a
population of 6.3 million including 1.4 million in the urban area. The city is rich in
natural resources and has major outputs of gold, talcum, marble and a range of
agricultural products, particularly apples, of which it is among the leading producers in



-114-                      ANNEX7
China. It is an important tourism center and has major sea fishery and aquaculture
operations.
Administrative and Institutional Framework
6.    The State Environmental Protection Committee (SEPC) is the highest level of
authority on environmental policy and includes the State Council and heads of all
relevant ministries and agencies. NEPA functions as the secretariat of SEPC and is
responsible for all aspects of environmental policy although it shares authority with other
agencies for certain natural resources. NEPA sets overall policies and regulations
governing the provincial and municipal EPBs, and implementation of environmental
policy is through the municipal and provincial EPBs, who are responsible for the
maintenance of environmental quality.
7.    The Shandong Provincial Govermnent has accorded priority to the cleanup of the
XRB and, accordingly, established in 1994 the Xiaoqing River Basin Environmental
Management Commission to develop and implement a long-term strategy to improve the
condition of the river. In addition to pollution control, the strategy addresses flood
control, irrigation, navigation, aquatic production and tourism.
Project Description
8.    The proposed project comprises a total of six components as follows:
(a)   Jinan Wastewater Collection System-construction of about 38 km of
trunk and secondary sewer networks to permit utilization of the capacity
(220 000 m3/day) of the existing wastewater treatment plant;
(b)   Jinan Water Supply-facilities for abstraction of water (up to 9.6 M3!
second) from the existing irrigation intake on the Yellow River, storage in
a new reservoir of capacity 46 million m3 and to transfer to existing water
treatment plants;
(c)   Weihai District Heating-construction of a new CHP plant of capacity
24 MW electricity and 120 MW heat, about 17 km of steam and 13 km of
hot water distribution networks, and 10 heat exchange stations;
(d)   Yantai District Heating-provision of 30 km of heating network, 42 heat
exchange stations and peak boiler plant of capacity about 112 MW;
(e)   Xiaoqing Basin Industrial Pollution Control Subloan Facility; and
(f)   Technical Assistance and Training.
Of these components only (a) to (d) involve physical works in the immediate term and are
therefore covered by this Environmental Assessment (EA). Separate EA reports were



-115 -                     ANNEX7
prepared for each component, which then were synthesized into a comprehensive project-
wide EA report.
Baseline Data
9.    Shandong is the second largest province in China and has the third largest
aggregate GDP; the per capita GDP is Y 5,747, approximately 1.5 times the national
average and the seventh highest of the provinces (excluding the three province status
cities of Beijing, Shanghai and Tianjin). Contributions to the GDP from agriculture,
industry and the tertiary sector are 20.2, 47.4 and 32.4 percent, respectively. The gross
agricultural output of Shandong is the highest of any province in China and the gross
industrial output ranks second after that of Jiangsu.
10.   Some 64 percent of the area of the province is mountainous or hilly and forest
cover is 20 percent. The province includes eight major lakes and nine major rivers, of
which the most important is the Huang He (Yellow River), which in the western part of
the province forms the boundary with Hebei. Water resources in the province average
200 m3/capita.
11.   The energy needs of the province are met almost entirely by coal, which is of
variable quality, with sulfur contents sometimes in excess of 2.5 percent. As a result
Shandong has the highest emissions (in mass terms) of SO2 of any of the provinces in
China.
Climate
12.   The climate of Shandong is classified as temperate monsoon; rainfall is low,
annual averages being between 550 and 950 mm, and concentrated in summer. Annual
average temperatures range between 11 and 14 C, temperatures decreasing from northeast
to southwest. The coldest month is January, with average temperatures ranging from -4
to 1 C, and the hottest month is July, with average temperatures between 24 and 27 C.
The average number of frost-free days ranges from 180 to 220 per year.
13.   The Xiaoqing River originates in the west of Jinan, the Provincial capital, and
flows a distance of 237 km, passing through a total of 5 cities and 18 towns, villages and
counties, before discharging to the Bohai Sea in Laizhou Bay in eastern Shandong.
Average annual rainfall in the basin is 619.5 mm, concentrated principally in the wet
season (July to September), which accounts for 50 to 60 percent of the total annual
rainfall. The mean flow in the Xiaoqing is 40.3 m3/second; much of the rainfall in the
basin recharges the shallow and deep aquifers that underlie the region.
14.   Both Weihai and Yantai have a continental monsoon climate, with annual average
temperatures of 12.3 and 13 C, respectively. Annual rainfall in the two cities averages
777 mm and 613 mm, respectively, the majority of which in each case occurs in summer.
The prevailing wind direction in Weihai is northwest and between south-southwest and



-116-                       ANNEX7
west-southwest in Yantai; average annual wind velocities are 5.6 m/second and 3.6 m/
second, respectively.
Water and Air Quality Standards
15.   The water quality standards appropriate in respect of water quality in the Xiaoqing
basin are those of the national Environmental Quality Standard for Surface Waters
(GB 3838-88). The National Standard defines water quality standards applicable to five
different classes of surface water with designated uses ranging from national nature
reserves (Class I); municipal water supply and fisheries protection (Class II); water
supply after treatment and recreation involving contact (e.g., swimming) (Class III);
industrial water supply and noncontact recreation (Class IV) to agriculture and industrial
cooling water (Class V). The mainstream Xiaoqing River is currently very heavily
polluted, with concentrations of some pollutants being more than 10 times the maximum
concentration allowed by the least stringent classification, Class V.
16.   The national ambient air quality standards (GB 3095-82) specify different air
quality standards for different classifications of land use.  The standards specify
maximum annual average, maximum daily average and maximum instantaneous
concentrations of SO2, TSP and NO, for three categories of land use;
(a)   Class I: Tourist, historic, conservation and sanitarium areas;
(b)   Class II: Urban residential, cultural and rural areas and places of historic
interest;
(c)   Class III: Industrial districts and heavy traffic areas.
Class I areas are designated by the State Government and Class II and III areas by locals
government.
17.   Xiaoqing River Basin Water Quality. Industrial development in the Xiaoqing
basin has caused a major decline in water quality, and the river is now in effect a
wastewater canal. The present total wastewater flow discharged to the Xiaoqing and its
tributaries is approximately 12.5 m3/second, of which 7.5m3/second are derived from
industry. Thus the dilution available for this wastewater is only a factor of about 3 on
even an annual average basis and much lower during the dry season. As a result
concentrations of COD exceed 200 mg/l, some 10 times even the least stringent Class V
standard, and dissolved oxygen is present only at the source and in minimal
concentrations in the lower reaches. A range of toxic or persistent organic chemicals
have been identified in the mainstream Xiaoqing.
18.   The main sources of pollution of the Xiaoqing are industrial wastewater
discharges and urban wastewater from a number of cities and counties, principally Jinan,
Zibo, Binzhou and Weifang, and from the Qilu petrochemicals complex, which is located
close to Zibo but discharges wastewater via a 60 km pipeline into the Xiaoqing close to



-117-                      ANNEX7
the outlet to Laizhou bay. The pollution loads to the Xiaoqing are shown in Table 1
below.
TABLE 1: POLLUTION LOADS TO THE XIAOQING RIVER
(tons/year)
Reach                           Total COD Load         Industrial COD Load
Jinan                               153,867                   122,714
Zibo                                117,864                   97,140
Binzhou                              31,216                    28,845
Dongying                             25,434                   24,826
Qilu Petrochemical                    8,848                    8,848
Weifang                              56,807                   53,983
TOTAL                            394,036                   336,356
19.   The industrial wastewater COD load, in total accounting for approximately 85
percent of the overall total load, is dominated by the loads associated with wastewaters
from two sectors of industry. The major polluting industry sector is the manufacture of
paper using straw as the raw material from which the pulp is produced. This sector
generates an aggregate COD load of approximately 211,000 tons/year, some 63 percent
of the total industrial COD load to the Xiaoqing and more than 50 percent of the overall
total COD load. The other important polluting sector is food and beverage production,
pollution from which is dominated by wastewaters from wineries and distilleries. The
sector in total accounts for 27 percent of the industrial COD load and 23 percent of the
overall load. Thus, these two sectors in aggregate account for more than 75 percent of the
overall load to the Xiaoqing and its tributaries and clearly these sectors must be a key
focus of any pollution control program for the Xiaoqing basin.
20.   These overall COD loads are extremely high, given the very limited water flows
in the Xiaoqing. The total COD load of 394,036 tons/year is equivalent to an average
concentration (based on the annual average flow of 40.3 m3/second and neglecting self-
purification) in the order of 300 mg/l. Such concentrations are understood to be
consistent with those measured in the upper reaches of the river in the Jinan region.
21.   A major factor affecting water quality in the upper reaches of the Xiaoqing is the
inadequate sewerage system in Jinan. A major wastewater treatment plant (with a
capacity of 220,000 m3/day) has been constructed, but this treatment capacity cannot be
utilized because of sewerage system deficiencies, which means that all Jinan wastewater
flows remain untreated.
22.   For the purposes of water quality management in the basin, the Xiaoqing River
has been divided into four main reaches-Jinan; Zibo-Binzhou; Dongying; and Weifang,
and 17 river sections. The former two reaches constitute the nontidal portion of the river,



-118 -                        ANNEX7
a total river length of 166 km, and the latter two (a total of 71 km) the tidal estuary. The
long-term (2000-10) water quality objectives for the Xiaoqing are as follows:
Water Quality Classification
Reach                        (GB 3838-88)
Jinan                             IV
Zibo-Binzhou                      III
Dongying-Weifang                  II
23.   Shandong EPB has made estimates of the assimilative capacity of the Xiaoqing,
based on a water quality model developed by the Shandong Environmental Protection
Design Institute (SEPDI) for dry-season flow conditions. Based on these estimates, the
EPB has also made preliminary estimates of the degrees of reduction in COD loads
entering the river that would be necessary to achieve the water quality objectives. The
projected and allowable COD loads for the year 2010 are as follows:
2010 COD Load to River Reach (tons/year)
Jinan      Zibo-Binzhou      Dongying-Weifang       Total
Projected /a            114,066        35,020               65,540          245,153
Allowable                 8,424         2,662                3,277           14,363
La Taking account of self purification and deposition in tributaries and lakes, the benefit of this may in
practice be less than expected because of resuspension of polluted material from the river bed during
the first rains following dry periods.
24.   These figures imply a need to reduce loads by more than 90 percent by 2010. In
practice, as may be seen from Table 1 above, the present total point source COD loads
before treatment are already in the order of 400,000 tons/year.
25.   The magnitude of the water pollution problems and the limited water resources of
the XRB highlight the importance of control of wastewater discharges on the basis of
pollution loads rather than solely on simple concentration-based discharge standards.
This has been recognized in the case of the Xiaoqing Basin for some years and the basin
was selected by NEPA in 1987 to participate along with 17 cities (including Jinan and
Zibo) in the trial implementation of a discharge permit system.
26.   This has had limited effectiveness, however, because the permit system adopted
by the Shandong EPB was goal rather than capacity-based. The EPB established short-
and medium-term goals for reductions in pollution discharges in Jinan, Zibo and the Qilu
Petrochemical Industrial Area based on the pollution loads from these areas. A greater
reduction was required of areas that contributed a greater proportion of the total load,
where economic conditions were better or where technical resources were available. In



-119-                      ANNEX7
particular, 37 enterprises discharging more than 85 percent of the COD load from Jinan
were required by the Jinan EPB to register the details of their discharges.
27.   The system has not achieved the desired effect for a number of other reasons,
including its application only to existing discharges. As a consequence pollution loads
have continued to increase in spite of the fact that wastewater volumes and COD loads
discharged per unit of industrial output (at constant prices) each declined by more than a
factor of 3 between 1986 and 1994.
28.   It has also been appreciated that to achieve pollution load reduction targets it
would necessary for industry to change to cleaner production processes. To implement
management strategies for pollution prevention and control in the Xiaoqing basin, the
Shandong Provincial Government has issued an order that seriously polluting industries
would be ordered to close, cease production or comply with pollution control within
deadlines. This pollution control may take the form either of end-of-pipe treatment or the
introduction of cleaner production technologies involving lower levels of pollution.
29.   Weihai and Yantai Air Quality. Weihai was designated the first Chinese
"Clean City" in 1990, but atmospheric pollution is increasing as a result of the rising use
of coal for domestic purposes and increasingly as a fuel for industry. Total coal
consumption in Weihai is currently in the order of 900,000 tons/year; and typical sulfur
contents of the coal are in the order of 1.7 percent. Apart from a small area in the city
center air quality in Weihai is Class II or better and that in the southern part of the city is
Class I. However, it is expected that the proposed industrial development in the high-
tech zone would cause a decline in air quality in this area to Class II and also a further
decline in the city center.
30.   Although more than 95 percent of the population of the city proper of Yantai use
gas as a domestic fuel, consumption of coal (with sulfur contents typically in the order of
1.2 percent) exceeds 1.5 million tons/year, the majority of which is consumed by
industry. As a result air quality (in terms of SO2 concentrations) is currently Class III in
an area of about 18 km2 and fails to meet even this standard in a further 12 km2 in the
center of the city.
Consideration of Alternatives
31.   For all components the concepts represent the only practical solutions. Where a
range of detailed options was available, the proposals adopted were those meeting the
required objectives at least cost.
Environmental Benefits
32.   The Project involves components aimed at substantially reducing discharges of
pollution to the XRB and to the atmosphere.  Accordingly, the balance of the
environmental impact of the project is substantially positive and the positive



-120 -                     ANNEX7
environmental benefits greatly outweigh the negative impacts. Environmental benefits of
the project components are described below.
33.   Jinan Wastewater Collection. The provision of enhanced wastewater collection
facilities in Jinan would result in the collection and subsequent treatment of a wastewater
flow of 220,000 m3/day, some 46 percent of the total urban wastewater flow. Treatment
of this flow would reduce the COD load from Jinan urban wastewater by 32,120
tons/year, some 20 percent of the total COD load to the Xiaoqing from the Jinan region,
with substantial reductions in the loads of other pollutants.
34.   This component would reduce the COD  concentration in the Xiaoqing
downstream of Jinan by almost 100 mg/l (approximately 45 percent), albeit only to a
level in excess of 130 mg/I, still more than six times even the Class V standard.
35.   Jinan Water Supply Intake. This component would sustain the use of the
Yellow River as a water resource for Jinan during the dry season and would reduce the
dependence on groundwater.  Groundwater is currently being abstracted at an
unsustainable rate in terms of its recharge; as a result the quality of groundwater is
declining, and the continued abstraction of groundwater in Jinan, with the associated
reduction in groundwater levels, threatens the flow of water in the springs for which Jinan
is famous. The scheme would yield a supply of approximately 400,000 m3/day, resulting
in an improvement in the quality of water entering supply serving a population of some
1 million.
36.   Weihai District Heating. The proposed No. 3 Thermal Power Plant in Weihai
would provide district heating and process steam for the developing high-tech industrial
zone in the south of the city, thereby substituting 29 existing boilers and avoiding the
provision of any new boilers and household heating stoves in the zone. This would result
in significant savings in coal consumption as a consequence of both economies of scale
and enhanced thermal efficiency of heat supply, with associated benefits of reduced
emissions of SO2 and TSP. These emissions would be reduced still further by the fact
that the combustion process employed at the power plant is a fluidized-bed system with
injection of limestone to remove SO2; in addition, the impact of the emissions at ground
level is further reduced by their discharge through a tall (100 m) stack compared with the
existing discharges from independent boilers and stoves at very close to ground level.
37.   As a consequence of these reductions in emissions, there would be significant
improvements in air quality both in the high-tech industrial zone and elsewhere in the
city. The environmental improvements associated with the project are shown in Table 2.
38.   Yantai District Heating. The proposed conversion of the Yellow Sea and Bohai
Sea Thermal Power Co. Ltd. power plant to a CHP system for extending district heating
in Yantai would replace about 200 existing boilers and 64,000 household stoves and
avoid the provision of any new such facilities. Coal consumption in the city is expected
to increase by almost 25 percent between 1994 and 2000, with associated worsening of
air quality.



-121-                           ANNEX7
39.    The project would reduce the growth in coal consumption to one-third this level
and would reduce emissions of SO2 and TSP by a corresponding amount. There would
be greater improvements in ground level air quality as a result of the discharge of
emissions from the peak heat supply boilers associated with the project via a tall stack
(100 m). The environmental benefits of the Yantai District Heating component are given
in detail in Table 2.
TABLE 2. ENVIRONMENTAL BENEFITS OF DISTRICT HEATING COMPONENTS IN 2000
City                   Reductions (tons/yr) in              Changes in area (km2) in
Coal use       Emissions of         >Class III     Class III    Class II
S02       TSP
Weihai                2,753      4,549     2,422         n.a.          -XX         -XX
Yantai              120,000      5,340     4,561          -24           -4          +6
Notes: 1. All benefits are expressed relative to the 2000 No Project case.
2. The relatively low reduction in coal use in Weihai in relation to the reductions in emissions is
due to the improved heating levels provided by the new facility and to the flue gas
desulfurization by limestone injection at the power plant.
3. The net increase in the area of Yantai in Class II is accounted for by the elimination of air
quality worse than Class III and reductions in the Class III area, air quality in each case being
improved to Class II.
4. N.a.-not applicable-no areas in Weihai would have air quality worse than Class III even in
the no project case.
Impacts and Mitigation
40.    Although the impact of the project is on balance  substantially  positive,
nevertheless, negative impacts have been identified in the EA process for all components
that require detailed analysis and mitigation measures. The principal impacts for each of
the individual project components are described below.
Jinan Wastewater Collection
41.    Construction Phase. The construction impact of the Jinan wastewater collection
project would be almost entirely during the construction phase. Excavation for the
installation of about 38 km of sewers would result in substantial quantities of spoil
material; however, the majority of this material would be used in other construction
projects in Jinan. A detailed spoil disposal plan would be prepared. Other impacts of the
project during construction include noise, dust and disruption to traffic and other urban
services. The impact would be reduced to the minimum practicable by controls on
construction practice.
42.    Sludge Disposal. The principal objective of the wastewater collection component
is to facilitate the effective use of the existing wastewater treatment plant, which is
currently limited by sewerage system deficiencies. When operating at design throughput,
the wastewater treatment plant would generate a total of some 53 tons (as dry solids) of



-122 -                      ANNEX7
sludge daily. Sludge would be appropriately treated and safely disposed principally
through codisposing to municipal sanitary landfills.
Jinan Water Supply Intake
43.   Resettlement. This project requires substantial land acquisition, both temporary
and permanent, totaling in excess of 8 km2 and resettlement of a total of 1,186 persons.
These issues are discussed in detail in Annex 6.
44.   Downstream Impact. The proposed mode of operation of the facility envisages
an abstraction of 9.65 m3/second during the highest flow period of July-September and of
8.65 m3/second during the remainder of the year. At some times of the year, it may not
be possible to sustain such an abstraction rate without adverse impact upon downstream
water uses or water quality. Under such conditions, abstraction rates would reduce or
abstraction would be suspended.
45.   Construction Phase. During construction, there would be a number of impacts
such as noise, dust, construction traffic and disruptions to land use and services; these
would be minimized, wherever possible, by using environmentally responsive
construction specifications, controls on construction practice through adequate site
supervision and by carefully scheduling construction operations. In particular, there
would be disruption to the road from Jinan to Dezhou; a temporary replacement road
would be constructed.
46.   Seepage Control. Groundwater in the area of the proposed reservoir is relatively
shallow and there is concern that leakage from the base of the reservoir could result in
rising groundwater levels and possibly even waterlogging of soils. In view of the high
evaporation rates, there is concern also in respect of salinization of soils. Two methods
of leakage control are therefore proposed. The reservoir would be lined with geotextile
membranes with appropriate blockwork protection and, in addition, a system of leakage
collection and discharge ditches would be constructed.
47.   Dredged Material Disposal.  The Yellow  River carries high silt loads,
particularly during high flow periods; silt loads contained in the water abstracted have
been estimated at almost 1.2 million m3 annually. Accordingly, it would be necessary to
remove silt from the water before it enters the reservoir to avoid capacity loss by siltation,
and a dedicated sedimentation basin is provided for this purpose. This sedimentation
basin would require dredging at intervals to sustain its operation. The dredged material
would be moved to a stockyard area where it would be kept moist to prevent dispersal of
fine sand material and covered to generate new agricultural areas. The Yellow River
Basin authorities and JMSC have built up extensive experience with the removal,
handling, and environmentally safe management of this silt.
48.   Control of Eutrophication.  Data for nutrient (nitrogen and phosphorus)
concentrations in the Yellow River indicate that the reservoir could be eutrophic.
Concentrations in the River are particularly high during the period when flows increase as



-123 -                      ANNEX7
a result of the first rains after prolonged dry periods (particularly at the beginning of the
wet season). It is proposed, as far as possible (resource considerations permitting), to
control nutrient loads entering the reservoir by restricting abstractions under these flow
conditions. In the reservoir, optimum levels for nitrogen and phosphorus are determined
to be 0.6 and 0.04 mg/l, respectively.
Weihai and Yantai District Heating
49.   Air Pollution Control. The principal impact of the district heating components
is the generation of boiler slag and fly ash residues. The ash contents of the coals used in
the cities are typically about 25 percent. Although in each case there is a substantial net
decrease in coal consumption, in all cases there would be a concentration of coal
consumption at a large facility rather than small-scale use at a large number of small
individual boilers and stoves. Thus, large amounts of residues would require disposal
from these facilities, and in the case of the Jinan and Weihai, the residues would contain
the products of flue gas desulfurization. It is proposed to use all residues from the power
plants and boilers in the manufacture of building materials at enterprises located nearby.
To minimize problems of dust during storage and transport of these residues, conveyors
would be covered and stockpiles would be kept moist.
50.   SPG  would, in parallel, undertake boiler upgrading and energy efficiency
programs to reduce SO2 and TSP emissions in Weihai and Yantai. This is expected to
contribute to overall air quality improvement.
51.   The power stations and boilers are located in urban areas, and in some cases, it
would be necessary to provide noise insulation and attenuation measures to ensure
compliance with urban noise standards. The construction of the distribution systems for
steam and hot water would generate spoil from excavation. However, given the general
pipework sizes it is not expected that quantities of excess spoil would be substantial.
52.   The impacts and their associated mitigation measures are listed in Table 3.

Implementation Program
53.   Based on the EA findings, SEPB has prepared an EA implementation program.
This program covers the above mitigation measures, ambient environment and emissions
monitoring, institutional arrangements, costs and progress reporting.

-135-                     ANNEX12
ANNEX 12: ENVIRONMENTAL POLLUTION PREVENTION
AND CONTROL
Introduction
1.    Shandong's industrial growth of nearly 17 percent per year over the past five
years has been accompanied by increasing discharges of wastewater, solid waste, and air
pollutants. An increasingly strict environmental regulatory regime has held waste
discharges below the overall growth rate, but wastewater and air polluting discharges
have still grown some 7 percent per year. Naturally, the impact of this growth varies with
location, industrial concentration and type of effluent. The candidate cities for the
Shandong Environment Project have the largest concentrations of industry, and some of
the most highly polluting, in the province: Jinan and Zibo industry discharges to the
Xiaoqing River, which is experiencing declining absorptive capacity, virtually rendering
it unusable for agriculture or fisheries.
2.   In the province as a whole, the pulp and paper industry remains the worst polluter,
responsible for 58 percent of all industrial water pollution and providing 20 of the top 45
polluters. Next comes the alcohol industry, with 19 percent of wastewater, and 1 1 of the
top 45 polluters. The metallurgy industry ranks third, with one company representing 3
percent of total industrial pollution. Other top polluters include a variety of chemical and
refinery plants.
3.    The XRB provides one measure of the relative impact of environmental pollution.
The water pollution in the river is mainly caused by organic pollutants, with serious
consequences for beneficial uses of the river. The point source pollution in the Basin
represents 94.8 percent of the total pollution load. About 85.4 percent is from industries
and 14.6 percent from urban sewage. The nonpoint pollution, while only 5.2 percent of
the pollution load, is nevertheless still significant.
4.    Analysis of pollution sources and abatement costs in Shandong demonstrates the
relatively low cost of addressing some pollutants at source. A significant reduction of
industrial COD, for example, is estimated to cost about Y 858 million investment. Some
281,400 kg COD would be removed by treating 173 million m3 wastewater a year. The
Environmental Pollution Control component of the project addresses these industrial
point sources.
5.    The component relies on a two-part strategy: (a) lending for a number of smaller
pollution prevention and control investments through a Xiaoqing River Basin Subloans



-136-                     ANNEX12
Facility (XRBSL), to be capitalized at $10 million, utilizing $5 million of proceeds of the
Bank loan, and an equal amount of local currency; and (b) action plans for the cleanup of
the Basin. This annex discusses in turn each part of the strategy.
Environmental Policy in Shandong Province
6.   In May 1988, the Implementation Plan for Pollution Prevention and Treatment in
the XRB was approved by the Provincial People's Congress Standing Committee. It
prioritized four actions:
* treating 31 high-polluting enterprises;
* construction of two municipal wastewater treatment plants in Jinan and Zibo;
* improving water quality by transferring water from the Yellow River and
Mada Lake;
v providing good quality drinking water in the seriously polluted areas.
So far 12 of the 31 enterprises have treated their wastewater discharge, the wastewater
treatment plant in Zibo (140,000 tons/day) is completed and in Jinan (220,000 tons/day)
is nearly completed, the Yellow River is contributing, on average, 1.5 m3/second of water
and drinking water is provided now to 360,000 people by drilling 237 deep wells and
building 10 oxidation ponds.
7.    At the end of 1995 and during 1996, Shandong Province issued new regulations to
strengthen water pollution prevention and control:
3 Notice on the Establishment of a Special Fund for Controlling Pollution
Generated from Pulp and Paper Enterprises, Breweries and Distilleries, No.
19.  This document requires enterprises producing pulp and paper,
monosodium glutamate (MSG), citric acid and alcoholic beverages to
contribute to a special fund, based on their annual production output, as long
as the concentration of pollutants in their wastewater exceeds the national
standards;
* Decision on Strengthening Water Pollution Prevention and Control, No. 31.
It sets a timetable for wastewater discharge control, indicating that by the end
of 1997 the key polluting industries located along the river basin should be in
compliance with national standards and by the end of 2000, all industrial
pollution sources should meet the standards; and,
* Provisional Measures for Collecting the Urban Wastewater Fee in Shandong
Province, No. 52. This document mandates the collection of urban wastewater
treatment fees from working units and individuals, located in the service area,



-137-                      ANNEX 12
to cover the construction, operating and maintenance costs of the centralized
treatment plants.
Pollution Fee Collection and Use in Shandong Province
8.    As one means of providing technical and financial assistance to help polluters to
bring their discharges within the pennitted loads, a 1982 Chinese environmental law
provided for the establishment of provincial, municipal and county environmental funds
financed by pollution levies. The levies originally provided grants for pollution control
investments in industrial and municipal projects, and 20 percent was earmarked for EPB
environmental monitoring and enforcement activities. A 1988 amendment to the law
stipulated that up to 50 percent of the fund income was to be loaned rather than granted to
enterprises in Shandong, and in 1990 SPG ruled that the fund could no longer provide
grants to industry, thereby enhancing the Polluter Pays Principle. By the end of 1994, the
total amount of loans made to enterprises was Y 449 million, implementing 1,064 projects
for pollution treatment and control.
9.   In Shandong, municipal and county EPBs collect pollution levy fees, while the
provincial, municipal and county EPBs jointly plan fee collection and utilization. The
finance bureau at each level of government holds the revenue collected, and disburses it
via local branches of the People's Construction Bank of China according to a fund
allocation plan provided by the EPBs.
10.   Fee rates have been established for wastewater discharges, waste gas emissions,
solid waste disposal and noise pollution. Fee collections rose from Y 19 million in 1991
to over Y 33 million in 1995, with over 70 percent of the collected fees used for industrial
pollution control and the remainder financing the EPBs' environmental monitoring and
enforcement work.
Environmental Policy for the Xiaoqing River Basin
11.  In 1988, a special organization was established by SPG-the Xiaoqing River
Basin Environmental Management Commission. It has no office of its own, but under its
leadership are two organizations with full-time staff:
*  the Xiaoqing River Basin Environment Leadership Group within the
Provincial Planning Commission, whose tasks are to compile comprehensive
plans for environmental management in the river basin and to coordinate
between the government agencies involved in the implementation of these
plans;
* the Xiaoqing River Basin Environmental Management Office within SEPB,
whose tasks, within the river basin, are to develop environmental regulations,
monitoring and inspecting environmental programs, enforcement and
participating in the development of comprehensive plans for environmental
management.



-138-                      ANNEX 12
12.   As a result of a law (Luzhengfa, No. 42, 1995) passed by SPG, some companies
have been closed, while 45 provincial enterprises and 55 enterprises below the provincial
level have been ordered to reduce their emissions before the end of 1997. The estimated
impact is a reduction of daily discharge of COD of 220 tons.
Pollution Fee Collection and Use in the Xiaoqing River Basin
13.   For the Xiaoqing River Basin area, the money collected from pollution levies is
shared between 24 accounts: 5 municipal EPBs, 18 county EPBs and the provincial EPB,
where it is mixed with levies from all other parts of the province. Per year, the 23
sublevel EPBs deal with a total of Y 130 million used specifically for pollution control
while, at provincial level, Y 40 million (1995) are available for the whole province. The
pollution levy funds of the municipalities along the river basin, that is Jinan, Zibo,
Weifang, Dongying and Binzhou, total Y 136 million. Y 76 million is used for
wastewater treatment.
14.   The Special Fund for Controlling Pollution Generated from Pulp and Paper
Enterprises, Breweries and Distilleries, mentioned above, would only contribute to
pollution control investments. The total amount that is collected by the Light Industries
Bureaus and the TVIE Management Bureaus would be returned to enterprises. The fees
are Y 100 per ton of pulp; Y 50 per ton of alcohol, MSG and citric acid; and Y 20 per ton
of beer based on annual output.
15.   Bank Group Experience in China with Environmental Funds. China still has
limited experience with environmental loan funds. The Bank Group has supported the
establishment of such funds under seven different projects and three of them have been in
operation for at least one year. Compared to domestically financed funds, the Bank
Group-assisted funds have been found to have the following advantages:
(a)   they typically provide a stronger framework for management, including
organization, staffing and operation regulations, and consciously seek
links with other environmental protection management measures such as
the promotion of pollution prevention programs;
(b)   they institute rigorous requirements and procedures for project preparation
and appraisal, ensuring a higher project success rate; and
(c)   they train staff of the fund offices in the technical and financial areas.
16.   One disadvantage of Bank-supported funds is that the more rigorous appraisal
procedures have been expensive compared to the size of the typical loan, which has been
under $1 million. Due regard needs to be given to modifications of the appraisal
procedures to bring down costs while maintaining quality.



-139-                      ANNEX12
Xiaoqing River Basin Subloans Facility
17.   The purpose of Xiaoqing River Basin Subloans Facility (XRBSL) is to strengthen
the existing Shandong pollution prevention and control program with a technically and
institutionally sustainable financing mechanism. The subloans would primarily assist
small-scale industrial enterprises within the Xiaoqing River Basin to control pollution
through waste minimization measures, modifications or renovations to existing plants to
reduce waste outputs, clean technology, or recycling waste generated during production.
Industrial upgrading projects designed to reduce the amount of pollutant discharge and to
save natural resources and energy, commercial waste recovery services and wastewater
treatment plants would also be considered by this facility. SEPB has identified a priority
list of Basin enterprises, and others among the 45 most polluting enterprises, to receive
preferential access to XRBSL.
18.   Organization and Financing of XRBSL. XRBSL would be a self-accounting
govermnent facility, with an initial capital equivalent of Y 83 million. The Bank loan
would provide $5 million and Shandong Province would contribute an equivalent sum
over three years (about Y 16.5 million in 1997, Y 12.5 million in 1998 and Y 12.5
million in 1999). While the size of the Bank contribution has been kept small, the
justification for Bank support for the facility derives from, first, the advantages listed
above.
19.   SEPB would prepare draft operations regulations for XRBSL, setting out the
criteria for subloans processing and approvals, the rules and regulations for management,
and defining the terms and conditions for loans. Disbursement against this component
can begin only after selection of a financial agent to act as the agent in handling loan
funds, and the signing of an agreement, acceptable to the Bank, with Shandong Province,
setting out the agency agreement. SEPB, with the cooperation of SFB, would deternine
the institutional structure and staff composition of the Subloans Management Office
(SMO) and approve its annual work plan and budget.
20.   The SMO would have up to 12 staff, to be recruited during a three-year period,
including specialists in environmental science and technology, industrial processing,
economics and finance, and administration. The director would be appointed by SPG,
and other staff would be locally recruited. The main role of SMO would be in investment
project planning, coordination between borrower and financial agent, review of project
feasibility, approval of subloans and supervision of project implementation.  The
financial appraisal would be the responsibility of the financial agent. The technical
appraisal would be contracted to design institutes by the financial agent.
21.   Project Selection.  Each application would be first reviewed by the local
industrial bureau and planning commission to ensure consistency with municipal
environmental planning. If the proposed investment appears feasible, the application
would be forwarded to SMO for further processing. SMO would lead an environmental
appraisal assessing the suitability of the pollution abatement measures proposed to the



-140-                      ANNEX 12
effluents produced in the enterprise. The financial agent would carry out a financial
appraisal, looking particularly at the appropriateness of the investment given the input
and output markets, the quality of enterprise management as demonstrated in their current
operating environment and a financial analysis to ensure the enterprise's ability to repay
the loan. The technical analysis would be carried out in accordance with the criteria
developed in a special training program, and review the designs for easily maintained and
operated systems well within the technical competence of enterprise personnel.
Project Management Procedures
22.   XRBSL operating procedures would include the following:
(a)   SMO would issue directives and solicitations for project proposals to the
priority-area EPBs and planning commissions;
(b)   With consent from the local industrial bureau, the enterprise would submit
a loan application to its EPB and planning commission;
(c)   If the project appears feasible, the local EPB would forward the loan
application to SMO for review and further processing. SMO would carry
out an environmental appraisal while the financial agent would make a
quick financial assessment of the enterprise;
(d)   With SMO concurrence, the enterprise would prepare a feasibility report
including engineering design, cost estimates, a waste minimization plan
prepared by a design institute with expertise in waste minimization, a
financial proposal with a time-bound investment plan, and an
environmental impact assessment;
(e)   Upon receiving the feasibility study, the financial agent would undertake a
detailed financial appraisal, and contract with a design institute to
undertake a technical appraisal;
(f)   After completion of the financial and technical appraisal, the financial
agent would prepare a comprehensive report, including the technical
appraisal carried out by the design institute, which, together with the
feasibility report, it would send to SMO with its observations and
recommendations;
(g)   After the project has been successfully appraised and approved by SMO,
the appraisal report and proposed loan conditions would be submitted by
SMO to the World Bank for no-objection. The Bank would provide
ex-ante review of the first three subloan projects and thereafter for each
subloan of over $300,000, with all other subloans subject to ex-post
review;



-141-                      ANNEX 12
(h)   SEPB, in conjunction with SFB, would be responsible for the final
approval of subloan projects. After approval, SMO would confirm the
loan to the enterprise, any cofinancing agencies and the financial agent;
(i)   SMO would take into account the forecast of the original waste
minimization audit when assessing the project implementation and focus
in particular on the no- and low-cost options implementation;
(j)   After satisfying itself as to the quality of a commissioned project, the
relevant bureau would issue a Certificate of Examination and Acceptance
to the enterprise;
(k)   The bureau in charge would submit examination and acceptance
documents for the project to SMO; and
(1)   SMO would separately assess whether the project meets the design
document requirements.  If it does not, SMO would arrange for
appropriate departments to intervene, seeking necessary amendments to
the project.
Project Appraisal
23.   For the technical appraisal of individual projects, the general criteria to be
considered would be: (a) the project's impact on the ambient environment; (b) a waste
minimization audit and compliance with environmental regulations and standards (EA),
involuntary resettlement (including preparation of a RAP; and (c) technical feasibility and
identification of the least-cost option.  Design institutes responsible for technical
appraisals would have undergone special training in waste minimization. This training
has been established with the assistance of the United Nations Development Programme
(UNDP) and the China National Cleaner Production Center.
24.   The financial appraisal must demonstrate that the enterprise, as a whole, would be
financially viable, including meeting a debt service ratio larger than 1.4 after the
proposed project reaches full production capacity. For joint waste treatment facilities, a
financing plan for the operation and maintenance of the facility would be required.
Project Financing Procedures Between Financial Agent and Borrower
25.   Once a subloan application is approved by SEPB/SFB, the financial agent would
execute the loan according to procedures described below:
(a)   The agent would confirm the project financing plan with the borrower, in
accordance with the loan agreement signed between Shandong Province
and the enterprise;
(b)   The enterprise would open an account with the agent;



-142-                      ANNEX 12
(c)   The agent would disburse funds upon receipt of statement of expenditure,
in the form of invoice or letter of credit. Normally, disbursement would
be made once a month;
(d)   The agent would supervise funds use by the enterprise. If project funds
are found to have been used for any purpose other than the approved
project, the agent would refuse further disbursement and notify SMO;
(e)   The agent would report to SMO quarterly on the financial status of loans
made to borrowers. The agent would also report emerging issues and
make suggestions for improvement as needed;
(f)   At project completion, the agent would finalize the financial accounting;
(g)   If projects fail to meet project date or design criteria, the agent shall notify
SMO; and
(h)   The agent would undertake the collection of loan principal, interest, late
payment penalties and fines.
Disbursement would be made through the agent from the account for XRBSL in SFB.
Control and Annual Audit of XRBSL
26.   The quality of waste minimization audit reports would be checked during the first
year of operation by the National Cleaner Production Center (NCPC), located in Beijing.
After this first year, an inspection panel involving NCPC, the World Bank and UNEP
would evaluate the audit quality and procedure.
27.   XRBSL would be audited each financial year by a qualified and independent auditor
acceptable to the Bank. The auditor is required to furnish a written report indicating the
extent to which the financial statements and supporting information provide a true and fair
view of the financial condition and performance of XRBSL. The auditor should also
provide a separate management letter following the completion of the audit on any
improvements required in the financial systems and controls and improved use of resources.
The audit reports and annual accounts should be forwarded to the World Bank within six
months of the end of the fiscal year.
Loans
28.   The aggregate amount of subloans made to any one enterprise shall not exceed the
equivalent of $500,000. The aggregate amount of all subloans from XRBSL made for
any one subproject shall not exceed the lesser of 50 percent of total estimated project cost
(excluding land), or 100 percent of the foreign currency cost. The total estimated cost of
each subproject shall not exceed $1 million. Loan maturity would be three to five years,
with up to two years of grace. SFB would bear the subloan credit risk, and the enterprise



-143 -                    ANNEX 12
the foreign exchange risk. The subloan interest rate would be no less than the standard
interest rate for LIBOR-based US dollar single currency loans plus a spread of 1.5 percent
per year and a commitment charge of 0.75 percent. Repayments to XRBSL would be
recycled for additional subprojects to the extent funds are not needed for repayment of the
Bank loan.
Institutional Development and Equipment Needs
29.   SMO personnel would undergo an extensive training program. Training courses
would include waste management, waste reduction technology, particularly resource
recovery/recycling and clean technology. Training and equipment for XRBSL would be
partly financed under the Management and Agency Strengthening component of the
Shandong Environment Project.



-144-                       ANNEX 13
ANNEX 13: MUNICIPAL FINANCES
ASSUMPTIONS FOR FINANCIuL PROJECTIONS
1.    The assumptions made when calculating the projections of the on-budget revenue
and expenditure statements of (a) Shandong Province; and (b) Jinan, Weihai and Yantai
Municipalities; for the period 1996-2003 are set out below. On-budget revenues are those
arising from taxes levied on enterprises operating in the these areas; off-budget revenues
consist of special fees to enterprises and are used chiefly for capital expenditures.
Revenue Forecast
2.    The actual (1992-95) on-budget revenue figures have been derived from data
provided by the provincial and municipal governments. Between 1992 and 1995, the
average annual increase in revenue was between 14 and 25 percent in current terms. In
1994, the Central Government restructured the tax system, bolstering its share. As a result,
there were marginal declines in revenue in 1994 from 1993, except for Jinan Municipality,
which posted a gain of 63 percent. To estimate future revenues, average annual increases in
current terms of 10 percent for Jinan, 25 percent for Weihai, and 15 percent for Yantai have
been assumed using 1995 as the base year.
Expenditure Forecast
3.    Historically, on-budget expenditures have registered between 72 and 99 percent of
on-budget revenues. There was little change in that ratio in 1994 when the tax system was
restructured (para. 2), except in Jinan Municipality where expenditures did not rise in
proportion to the gain in 1994 revenues. To estimate future expenditures, the ratio of
expenditures to revenues is assumed to be generally between 72 to 99 percent of revenues.
4.    The following tables summarize projected revenue and expenditure data from 1996
to 2003 for the Municipalities of Jinan, Weihai and Yantai, the main beneficiaries of project
investments, and Shandong Province. Projected project expenditures are also included.

ANNEX 14: FINANCIAL ANALYSIS ASSUMPTIONS
A. JINAN WATER SUPPLY COMPANY
General
1.    The financial projections from 1995 to 2003 for Jinan Water Supply Company
(JWSC) were produced in conjunction with JWSC's financial staff and project
management staff.
2.    Inflation and Exchange Rates: Yearly general domestic inflation rates used in
the projections are: 6.2 percent in 1997, 5.8 percent in 1998, and 5.5 percent thereafter.
Price contingency allowances on the foreign costs of Bank-financed projects are expected
to average 2.3 percent a year from 1997 to 2003. It is assumed that exchange rate
adjustments would, on average, maintain purchasing power parity during the projection
period. The initial exchange rate is Y 8.3/$1.0.
3.    Financial Covenants: Total revenues should cover (a) operating expenses before
depreciation plus debt service coverage plus working capital increases; (b) allow for a
debt service coverage ratio of at least 1.3 times; and (c) contribute a minimum 20 percent
(on a three-year average basis) to capital investment.
Income Statement Assumptions
4.    Water Sales Revenue: Is based on average tariff and average water sales volume
projections. The average tariff growth rate is set so that sales revenue would meet
operating ratio, contribution to capital investment and debt service coverage covenants.
Water sales volume is set as the minimum of projected demand and projected supply
levels. Projected demand is set as the greater of projected usage on a per capita basis or
projected usage on a number of connections basis. Population growth rates and
connection growth rates are based on municipal planning statistics. Capacity expansion
plans are provided by JMWC.
5.    Average Tariffs: The average water prices in yuan per m3 (net of Water Supply
Fund and Public Utility Tax) in current terms during the implementation period for
JWSC are as follows:
1997       1993       1999      2000       2001       2002       2003
0.71      0.80        0.86       0.90      0.99       1.04        1.14
6.    Tariffs: The current residential, commercial and industrial tariffs in Jinan are
Y 0.50/m3, Y 1.30/m3, Y 0.80/m3, respectively. On top of the basic tariff, a Water Supply



-147 -                     ANNEX 14
Fund fee and Public Utility Tax are collected on the water bill on behalf of the
government, which adds approximately Y 0.10-0.20 to each bill.
7.    Sales Taxes: JMWC would be subject to a composite sales tax of 6.6 percent of
gross sales revenue, which includes net value-added tax (VAT) payable to the Central
Government and education and infrastructure taxes payable to Jinan Municipal
Government (JMG).
8.    Personnel: Operation and maintenance personnel are expected to increase to and
remain at a level of 77 staff/1,000 connections. Wages are expected to increase at the rate
of general domestic inflation plus 2 percent.
9.    Electricity: Expenses are projected to grow in real terms, averaging 8.0 percent
per year. It is JWSC's largest operating expense.
10.   Materials:  Expenses grow from the current base at the combined rate of
domestic inflation and capacity expansion.
11.   Maintenance: Expenses increase at the rate of domestic inflation.
12.   Other Expenses: Increase at the rate of general domestic inflation.
13.   Selling Expenses: Are primarily the wages of meter-reading staff. Staff levels
are not expected to increase, but wages are expected to increase at the general rate of
domestic inflation.
14.   Administration: Expenses are comprised largely of pension, medical costs and
management salaries. JWSC plans to keep the level constant in nominal terms.
15.   Depreciation: Composite depreciation rates for JMWC are assumed to be 7.5
percent for assets with a life of less than 15 years and 4.5 percent for assets with a life
greater than 15 years.
16.   Financial Charges: The interest payable on outstanding long-term and short-
term loans.
17.   Nonoperating Income: Comprised of (a) income from JWSC's subsidiaries and
(b) deferred income contributions to nonoperating income (see Other Sources).
18.   Income Taxes: JWSC is expected to pay 33 percent of profit before income tax.
Funds Flow Statement
19.   Long-Term Loan Borrowing: Follows the disbursement profile for this project,
plus disbursements for JMWC's existing loans.
20.   Equity Infusion: JMG capital grants are recognized as deferred income, not
equity.
21.   Other Sources: Government capital contributions to the project. The grants are
recorded as deferred income until asset depreciation begins, at which time deferred



-148 -                      ANNEX 14
income is applied to the income statement as nonoperating income at the same rate as
depreciation.
22.   Fixed Asset Investments:  Based on expenditures for this project and for
JMWC's concurrent network expansion plans. Other investments include (a) other water
supply capacity expansion projects and (ii) replacement investment.
23.   Increases in Working Capital: The excess, or otherwise, of the current year's
current assets (net of cash), less the excess of the previous year's current assets (net of
cash) over current liabilities.
24.   Total Financial Charge: The proceeds of the IBRD loan are assumed to be
onlent by JMG to JMWC at the standard rate for LIBOR-based US dollar single currency
loans plus 1 percent (6.92 percent per year at the time of appraisal), and 0.75 percent per
year commitment charge, over 15 years, including 5 years of grace. Interest is paid
annually; interest during construction is not capitalized.
25.   Long-Term Loan Repayment: Amortization of loans would be on the basis of
equal payments of principal. JMWC would bear their respective foreign exchange risks.
JMG would provide the local counterpart funds as capital grants so no new loans for the
project are anticipated.
26.   Dividend: No dividend disbursement is planned.
27.   Cash Changes: Calculates the balance sheet cash and short-term marketable
securities balance for the current year. Cash buildups would be applied to future
investment projects.
Balance Sheet
28.   Accounts Receivable: Assumed to be 30 days of billings.
29.   Doubtful Receivable: 0.5 percent of accounts receivable.
30.   Inventory: Projected at 1 year of materials and maintenance expense, due to their
policy of undertaking annual discounted bulk purchases of supplies.
31.   Other Accounts Receivable: Comprised mainly of accounts owing JWSC's
engineering/construction subsidiary. It is expected to remain constant in nominal terms.
32.   Work-in-Process: For the project, assets reflect the implementation schedule.
33.   Accounts Payable:  Assumed to be 60 days of materials and maintenance
expense.
34.   Other Accounts Payable: Comprised largely of Water Supply Fund, connection
fees and construction taxes owing to the government. It is expected to remain constant in
nominal terms.



-149 -                      ANNEX 14
35.   Other Current Liabilities:  Wages payable and advances from  JWSC's
customers.
36.   Long-Term Loans: Comprised of the World Bank loan, a Construction Bank
loan, and a Municipal Water Supply Fund 0 percent loan.
37.   Equity: Remains at existing equity levels.

-152 -                      ANNEX 14
B. JINAN MUNICIPAL DRAINAGE COMPANY
General
1.    The financial projections from  1997 to 2003 for Jinan Municipal Drainage
Company (JMDC),were produced by its financial staff in conjunction with company
management and planning staff. The projections are in current Yuan million.
2.    Inflation and Exchange Rates: Yearly general domestic inflation rates used in
the projections are 6.2 percent in 1997, 5.8 percent in 1998, and 5.5 percent thereafter.
Price contingency allowances on the foreign costs of Bank-financed projects are expected
to average 2.3 percent a year from 1997 to 2003. It is assumed that exchange rate
adjustments would, on average, maintain purchasing power parity during the projection
period. The initial exchange rate is Y 8.3/$1.O.
3.    Financial Covenants: Total revenues should (a) cover operating expenses plus
the greater of depreciation or debt service and (b) debt service coverage should be at least
1.3.
Income Statement Assumptions
4.    Wastewater Sales Revenue: Based on average tariff rates and wastewater sales
volumes. The average tariff growth rate is set so that sales revenue would meet operating
ratio and debt service coverage covenants. In JMDC, projections of wastewater sales
volumes are assumed to be 80 percent of projected water sales volume. In addition, the
Water Conservation Office collects revenues from industry based on annual groundwater
extraction quotas (80 percent of 91.25 million mi3) multiplied by the average wastewater
tariff and passes this revenue on to the drainage company. Average 1997 wastewater
3~~~~~~~~~~3
tariff is Y 0.33/m3.
5.    Average Tariffs. The average prices in yuan per m3 in current terms during the
implementation period for JMDC are as follows:
1997       1998       1999       2000       2001        2002       2003
0.33       0.49       0.50       0.50       0.50        0.50       0.52
6.    Tariffs. The current residential, commercial and industrial tariffs in Y/m3 of
wastewater disposal in Jinan are 0.15, 0.54, and 0.39, respectively.
7.    Personnel: Operation and maintenance personnel are expected to increase to and
then level off at 12 staff/1,000 connections. Wages are expected to increase at the rate of
general domestic inflation plus 2 percent ann'ually.
8.    Electricity: Expenses are projected to grow in real terms, averaging 8.0 percent
per year. This is JMDC's largest expense. Electricity primarily is used to run pumping
stations and aerators, before the wastewater treatment plant becomes operational.



-153 -                      ANNEX 14
9.    Materials:  Expenses grow from the current base at the combined rate of
domestic inflation and capacity expansion rates.
10.   Maintenance: Expenses increase at the rate of domestic inflation.
11.   Depreciation: Composite depreciation rates for JMDC are assumed to be 4.5
percent.
12.   Sales Taxes: JMDC would be subject to no VAT or other sales taxes.
13.   Other Expenses: Increase at the rate of general domestic inflation.
14.   Selling Expenses: JMDC is not expected to have any selling expenses, since
wastewater is directly charged against the water bill and is collected by the water
company on behalf of JMDC.
15.   Administration: Expenses are primarily management salaries.
16.   Financial Charges: The interest payable on outstanding long-term and short-
term loans.
17.   Income Taxes. JMDC is not required to pay income taxes.
Funds Flow Statement
18.   Long-Term Loan Borrowing: Follows the disbursement profile for this project,
plus disbursements for JMDC's existing loans.
19.   Equity Infusion: JMG is expected to contribute its capital grants as deferred
income instead of equity.
20.   Other Sources: The government's capital contribution to the project. The grants
are recorded as deferred income until asset depreciation begins, at which time deferred
income is applied to the income statement as nonoperating income at the same rate as
depreciation.
21.   Fixed Asset Investments: Based on expenditures for this project only.
22.   Increases in Working Capital: The excess, or otherwise, of the current year's
current assets (net of cash), less the excess of the previous year's current assets (net of
cash) over current liabilities.
23.   Total Interest Expenses: The proceeds of the IBRD loan are assumed to be
onlent by JMG to JMDC at the standard rate for LIBOR-based US dollar single currency
loans plus 1 percent (6.92 percent per year at the time of appraisal), and 0.75 percent per
year commitment charge, over 15 years, including 5 years of grace. Interest is paid
annually; interest during construction is not capitalized.
24.   Long-Term Loan Repayment: Amortization of loans would be on the basis of
equal payments of principal. JMDC would bear the respective foreign exchange risk.



-154 -                      ANNEX 14
Also includes repayment on an existing Austrian Government loan used to construct the
water treatment plant.
25.   Dividend: JMDC plans to distribute no dividends.
26.   Cash Changes: Calculates the balance sheet cash and short-term marketable
securities balance for the current year.
Balance Sheet
27.   Accounts Receivable: Assumed to be 46 days of billings because there is about a
15-day lag between when the water company collects the revenues and when the revenues
are passed to JMDC.
28.   Doubtful Receivable: 2.98 percent of accounts receivable.
29.   Inventory: Projected at four months of materials and maintenance expenses.
30.   Work-in-Process: For the project, assets reflects the implementation schedule.
31.   Accounts Payable:  Assumed to be 60 days of materials and maintenance
expense.
32.   Other Accounts Payable:  Expected to remain constant during project
implementation.
33.   Long-Term Loans: Comprised of World Bank and Austrian Government loans.
34.   Equity:  Equal to the Government's contribution of the existing wastewater
treatment plant.

C. DISTRICT HEATING COMPANIES
General
1.    The financial projections for Weihai Botong Heat and Power Co. (WBHPC) and
Yantai Heat Supply Co., Ltd. (YHSC) were produced in conjunction with company
management, financial and planning staffs.
2.    Inflation and Exchange Rates: Yearly general domestic inflation rates used in
the projections are, 6.2 percent in 1997, 5.8 percent in 1998, and 5.5 percent thereafter.
Price contingency allowances on the foreign costs of Bank-financed projects are expected
to average 2.3 percent a year from 1997 to 2003. It is assumed that exchange rate
adjustments would, on average, maintain purchasing power parity during the projection
period. The initial exchange rate is Y 8.3/$1.0.
3.    Financial Covenants: Total revenues should cover (a) operating expenses plus
the greater of debt service or depreciation, and (b) debt service coverage of at least 1.3
times.
Income Statement Assumptions
4.    Power Sales: WBHPC is a combined heat and power company. It sells all
excess power generated to the local power grid at existing local prices adjusted annually
for inflation.
5.    District Heating, Cooling and Steam Sales: YHSC sells only district heating,
while WBHPC also sells steam and district cooling. District heating, cooling and steam
average tariffs are set proportionately to the heat used in their production and at levels
that would achieve financial covenants. District heating volumes are set at demand
levels, with steam absorbing the remaining available energy supply.
6.    Average Tariffs: The average prices in current terms for WBHPC are:
1997    1998    1999    2000    2001    2002    2003
Heating, Y/m2              -    24.00    24.00    24.00    24.00    26.40    26.40
Cooling, Y/GJ              -        -    13.31    25.58    25.58    28.14    28.14
Steam, Y/t                 -    34.13    34.13    34.13    34.13    37.55    37.55
Power, Y/kWh               -     0.46     0.46    0.46     0.46     0.51     0.51
7.    Average Tariffs. The average prices in current terms for YHSC are:
1997    1998    1999    2000    2001    2002    2003
Heating, Y/m2          23.53    23.53    23.53    23.53    23.53    24.71    24.71
8.    Personnel:  Salaries and wages of operation and maintenance personnel are
expected to increase to and then level off at 10 and 5 staff/l,000 connections in Weihai,



-157-                       ANNEX14
and Yantai, respectively. Wages are expected to increase annually 2 percent over the
general domestic inflation rate.
9.    Electricity: Expenses are projected to grow in real terms, averaging 8 percent per
year.
10.   Materials:  Expenses grow from the current base at the combined rate of
domestic inflation and capacity expansion rates. Heat is YHPC's main purchase; coal
and fuel are WBHPC's.
11.   Maintenance: Expenses increase at the rate of domestic inflation.
12.   Depreciation: Composite depreciation rates are as follows:
WBHPC, %     YHSC, %
Fixed asset life, <15 years  4.8           5.0
Fixed asset life, >15 years  7.0           7.0
13.   Sales Taxes: The district heating companies would be subject to the following
composite VAT, education and infrastructure taxes:
WBHPC       YHSC
Sales Tax, %    9.0         6.75
14.   Other Expenses: Increase at the rate of general domestic inflation.
15.   Selling Expenses: None are anticipated.
16.   Administration: Expenses are primarily management salaries. Management
levels are not expected to increase during the implementation period, but salaries are
expected to increase at the general rate of domestic inflation.
17.   Financial Charges: The interest payable on outstanding long-term and short-
term loans.
18.   Nonoperating Income: Deferred income contributions to nonoperating income
(see Other Sources).
19.   Income Taxes: Assumed to be 33 percent of profit before income tax.
Funds Flow Statement
20.   Long-Term Loan Borrowing: Includes World Bank project loans. No other
loans are required.
21.   Equity Infusion:  With the exception of Yantai, Shandong Government has
decided to account for government capital contributions as deferred income.



-158-                       ANNEX14
22.   Other Sources: Government capital contributions to the project. The grants are
recorded as deferred income until asset depreciation begins, at which time deferred
income is applied to the income statement as nonoperating income at the same rate as
depreciation.
23.   Fixed Asset Investments: All district heating companies only have project-
related fixed assets.
24.   Increases in Working Capital: The excess, or otherwise, of the current year's
current assets (net of cash), less the excess of the previous year's current assets (net of
cash) over current liabilities.
25.   Total Interest Expenses: The proceeds of the IBRD loan are assumed to be
onlent by Weihai Municipal Government and Yantai Municipal Government to their
respective district heating companies at the standard rate of LIBOR-based US dollar
single currency loans plus 1 percent (in total, 6.92 percent per year at the time of
appraisal), and 0.75 percent per year commitment charge, over 15 years, including 5 years
of grace. Interest during construction is paid annually.
26.   Long-Term Loan Repayment: Amortization of loans would be on the basis of
equal payments of principal. Each project utility would bear their respective foreign
exchange risk.
27.   Dividend: No dividends are anticipated.
28.   Cash Changes: Calculates the balance sheet. cash and short-term marketable
securities balance for the current year.
Balance Sheet
29.   Accounts Receivable: WBHPC is 30 days; YHSC is 30 days.
30.   Doubtful Receivable: 1.0 percent for both Weihai and Yantai.
31.   Inventory:  Projected to be 45 and 30 days of materials and maintenance
expenses in Weihai and Yantai, respectively.
32.   Work-in-Process: Reflects the project implementation schedule.
33.   Accounts Payable: WBHPC's and YHSC's are 30 days.
34.   Other Current Liabilities: None is assumed.
35.   Deferred Income: A long-term liability account housing government capital
contributions (see Other Sources).
36.   Long-Term Loans: WBHPC and YHSC have only World Bank loans.
